26110	1	Crisis of drought and desertification: this is why revolutionary ecology is needed
26110	3	The drought has hit Italy with a new and stronger wave: the rivers are dry, the waters flourish, and agriculture suffers – from north to south – for the moisture of the land and sudden attacks of parasites and cavalettes, as is happening these days in the inner areas of Sardinia. This is not a biblical scenario but the torride Italian spring-summer of 2022. What should a nation be doing by will and not by fatalism? Here is a reflection on the topic.
26110	5	Desertification and Desertification
26110	7	As you can already imagine, the problem is more serious and articulated than the simplistic narration that environmentalists are doing compared to the water emergency. The solph is always the same, but it doesn’t help... rather, saying that the antropization and human work cause the climate disturbance that on unified networks is denounced almost daily means offering a decisive aid to the desert. The problem, it seems obvious to say, but it’s good to repeat it, is first and foremost political – and with politics I mean what the highest can be attributed to this term. But first let’s see what’s going on, and let’s raise some myth: when we talk about droughts the thought goes immediately to the summer period, the season without or with little rain for excellence. And in general, it is so, because it has always been so. At least since Somebody or something has pushed our planet into the dancing of rotation and oscillation around the Sun. Dryness is not a summer event, or better, it finds its destructive foam in the summer. In fact, the problem is of the autumn and/or winter period because in these periods, when land and waterfalls should be “resisted” with the water needed to cope with the heat, there is instead that lack of rain that the most stupid affirm shockingly in the summer. In particular, the snow is important to accumulate in quantities on the mountains, in order to then release the water more slowly during the spring dissolving phase. It is therefore counted that the causes of drought, especially in northern Italy, will be searched more on the Padana plateau, since as it should be known thanks to a school geographical atlante all the so-called affluents of the left of the Po (Mincio, Adda, Ticino, Oglio etc.) are of ice origin, i.e. their scope is regulated by the seasonal breakdown of the alpine glaciers. The same speech for the great lakes as the one of Garda and Como, the same speech for the great non-affluent rivers of the Po which, however, swim the whole northeast, such as the Adige, the Isonzo and the Piave. It’s a good idea to be able to do this, but it’s a good idea to be able to do this.
26110	9	Question of Will
26110	11	Before facing a more philosophical than practical discourse, it is useful to make historical accents, at least for the honor of the truth, both on the so-called climate question and on the avant-garde works carried out by Italy at the beginning of the last century. Let’s give a few reference points to understand what we’re talking about: the climate issue has as the main topic the Earth’s temperature rise, which is an objective data as a result of numerous scientific findings. However, the perception that we have thanks to media over-exposition is that the temperature is rising and is continuing to rise by several degrees. In fact, we know that since the year when the temperatures began to be recorded scientifically and objectively, that is, from 1880, 140 years ago, the temperature on Earth has risen by 0.9 degrees. To this fact it must be added that around the middle of the 800s a period defined small ice age, which began in the middle of the 1400s, has ended; it goes by itself, as the name suggests that during these centuries the earth has experienced a period of cooling especially in the northern hemisphere: we have witnesses of glaciates that have allowed to walk on the Tamigi. It is a natural consequence, always through that “touch” that has given the way to the oscillation of this geoid called Earth, that from the end of the “small” ice period the temperatures have gone hand by hand up. Not to mention the great ice periods that we know have been events of geological scope, the last “only” 14,000 years before Christ. A needle beat for natural cycles of such a wide scope. From this objective data, however, there are two currents of thought to say unsubjective, at the limit of fatalist superstition. I trust the words of the doctor. Guglielmo Pannullo, who in an article for the 2020 Student Block well exposed these currents: “The skeptics and catastrophists – he explains – have two diametrally opposite points of view on the causes of global warming, and until a few years ago the discussion was mainly related to the Anglo-Saxon world. The full of discussion is the reason for this increase, not the amount. The role of the information world and the lobbies around the topic has led to the polarization of the positions and the formation of these two opposite spheres. As regards the skeptics – continues Pannullo – it is to the position of Prof. Zichichi, of which a few months ago a interview for Il Primato Nacional came out, who claims that the models today on the prediction of climate change are unpredictable, since the climate is a phenomenon that has so many variable factors that cannot be absolutely predicted with a mathematical model. As a result, he believes that the causes of global warming are linked to external activity on Earth, such as the solar, and yet not because of man. Globally, however, the credibility of the skeptical component, in some cases, has been put into strong debate as a result of the discovery that some exhibitors or supporters of global non-heating have been consultants of oil companies such as the Exxon, the Shell the Texaco etc. On the contrary, the catastrophic component attributes the responsibility of climate change to man, seeing in the excess CO2 and in the climate emissions the causes of global warming. The Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change) is a group of scientists who do not monitor environment or climate but study scientific publications, research products and report with a period of more or less five years. This latest 2014 report highlights how most scientists believe that humans are likely to be the cause of global warming.”
26110	13	It is therefore clear, thanks to this exhaustive explanation, how serious the environmental fact is a problem of perspectives, polluted without too many turns of words by a vision of the Jewish-Christian world (“Be fertile and multiply, fill the earth and reside it, dominate the fish of the sea and the volatile of the sky and every living striking on the earth” – Genesis 1,22) which contains the separation between man and cosm that comes through the secularization of the West to the capitalist and Marxist vision: that materialist, where the environment is different, is part of the capital, exploits the value of use and makes materially useful all that surrounds us. But the problem then – you’ll say – are men. This is not the case, because as much as catastrophists and hyppie can say, man is the decisive ecological agent for the re-balance of ecosystems.
26110	14	The solution is man.
26110	16	The solution is man. The solution is politics. If man is an animal, ordered in the cosmos together with all living things, he is for sure a political animal, i.e. community, solidarity, aggregation, technical and historical. Our nature deprived of a predestined habitat (such as the oceans for the plancton) moves us towards the organization of our space according to our political instinct. Couple, family, tribe, village, city, region, state, nation, empire... are all forms of organization not only social, but above all natural. Or rather, let’s stop thinking what is social and political as something distinct and separated from our lives, separated and enemy of nature. The first step of revolutionary ecology is to reject the schemes of the homo oeconomicus according to which the main characteristics of a man are the rationality (understood in precipuous sense, especially as precision in calculation) and the exclusive interest in the care of his own individual interests. Consumption, intense production, exploitation of the environment and precarious work are non-cause effects. We also reject the illuminist myths of the good wild that brings with it that kind of biological racism that considers the industrial society higher than that tribal, but is moved by the good feelings of bringing the tribes to their level by force. The problem is ideological: if one considers the problem only as a fatalist key “it’s forcibly so”, then the desert will continue to advance and harass our land. Let’s go to the problem of drought.
26110	17	A political problem
26110	19	After the due premise, always useful to this kind of speech that moves on ideologically mined fields, we pass to our water crisis, from the problem to the source. The problem, solved by the philosophers, is of political will that acts on the national territory to support it, modify it and improve it. Italy – at least over the past 80 years – has abandoned any prospects of industrial, energy, agricultural, naval, demographic and educational power. A perspective that brings with it the necessary corollary of infrastructure and laws that can ensure that power manifests in the cities as well as in the metropolities. The mountains are populous, the cities explode, the work is precarious and promises not land and roots but wealth, denatality kills us, the school is precarious. Dryness is a symptom of our sick society: an unhealthy people turn their land into a desert, but above all by renouncing to modify the land, to work on the waters, silk and by renouncing a regulated urbanization they allow the desert to manifest themselves. If man is not good, if he is hysterical, consumer, evanescent, exploited and ill, how do we claim that his home and his environment are better? Nature is our mirror: try to enter a forest alone, at night; you will see that it will be filled with the spirit with which we have entered: scary if we are not balanced, welcoming if we bring consciousness with us. It would therefore be the first duty of a revolutionary ecology to work on men, starting from an absolute principle that coats with the global vision of progress theories: “criminal is everything that has as effect to eradicate a human being or to prevent it from putting roots.” As a result, the rest comes: from how much has Italy abandoned the support to bonification consortiums, to landing works, to strategic plantations of office plants and forests, to urban planning of urban and rural centers, to energy independence first local and then national? Italy must return to a geographical thought, take back the map of its territory and have a 360° look at the whole territory. Dryness is combated by favouring waterways, working on reserve and means of aid to agriculture in an economic context voted for healthy work and not for intense exploitation of goods and landscapes. Healthy work for workers, according to the legislation that the pioneers of the third Italian road left us, healthy environment as we were taught by the ecological works carried out by Italy during the malignant twenty of the last century, both on its soil and on the colonies. And then again to look for water, like the ancient rabdomans, again to study the wealth of our soil and our seas in search of new resources. At least for the future there is hope, because from a digital generation the highest number of subscribers to agricultural addresses and environmental faculty has gone out. Imagine is the most natural act that can be, then we must give a reason to live here, on this earth and under this heaven. They are not easy solutions, they have the same scope as a geological cataclysm, but it is good to start talking about them and open concrete revolutionary agenda, which already now risks to overcome the delay caused by the senile dementia that afflicts us as a people and civilization. This is not an abstraction, but an impellent need.26111

26141	1	Science is not a dogma.
26141	3	It is not only typical of the No vax rhetoric, falling in the error are also many Pro vax. People who accuse the government and science of lying for the simple fact that they have changed approach by changing the context. For example: “You’ve said that the vaccine prevents infection, and instead.” It was true, it was said. But it was said when the possible infection concerned the variant Alpha, which however, and this was also said, had at least a 10% chance of “bucking” the vaccines. And, after the Alpha, it was said for the Delta variant. It was not false, it was true. As it is true that Omicron is different from the variants of Covid that have preceded it: in fact, it also infects vaccinated people. It makes them less infectious than unvaccinated, for less time and almost completely avoids hospitalizations. It contains them. Is this the sign that governments lie? Is it the proof that science has nothing to do with truth? But not everything is predictable. Things change, as the scientific evidence changes. Philosopher Karl Popper wrote important pages to clarify how the research of the scientific truth consists in the progressive elimination of errors. The assumption is that the error is hardly avoided at the beginning. So Popper argued that in the scientific world, as in everyday life, everything is true until its opposite is proven true. This is the liberal method. Why do we do so much to accept it? Because we are naturally inclined to a dogmatic vision. If we were not, we would not be divided for fifty years between the supporters of the Communist Party and those of the strongest Catholic Party in the West. There are two dogmatic parties. If we were not, those of our co-owners called “catto-communists” would not consider it natural to summarize two dogms, rather than to eliminate them. There is, therefore, an anthropological data to explain the refratarity of many in accepting the complexity of life and the falsehood of the Word. They a certain inclination to Messianism, to prejudice, to conspiracy and to blind faith. The same blindness of those faced with intensive therapies fills 80% of that 15% of non-vaccinated citizens is able to draw the amounts. But in this case to the anthropological data summarizes the negative effects of a school system unlikely to transmit to the men of tomorrow the rudiments of logic and mathematics of ever.

26158	11	“Thro the years – explains Gianni Cipriano – my approach has also changed: between 2013 and 2016 the perception of populism was different, I myself preferred to photograph the socio-economic condition of Italy looking at the citizens, their difficulties, and for this there was more passion and even more anger in my work. 26183	1	How Brazil is saving the world from a catastrophic food crisis
26183	3	The author of the article, Augusto Zimmermann, is a professor and rector of the Faculty of Law at the Sheridan Institute of Higher Education in Perth. He is also chairman of the Western Australian (Wa) Legal Theory Association and was a member of the Wa Law Reform Committee from 2012 to 2017. Zimmermann is a contractual professor at the University of Notre Dame in Australia and is co-author of several books, including Covid-19 Restrictions and Compulsory Vaccination: A Perspective on the State of Law (Connor Court).
26183	5	Brazil is the fourth largest food producer in the world and is fully self-sufficient in terms of basic foods: it is ranked as the world’s first producer of bananas, cacao, manioca, coffee, corn, rice, soy and sugar. And although most of these products are consumed in the domestic market, a significant part is also exported, including orange, palm oil, needle, arachides and tea, but also much more.
26183	7	However, the problem is that Brazil needs a constant supply of fertilizers to feed its powerful agricultural industry. And the country’s largest international supplier of fertilizers is Russia, which accounts for 44% of the total used by Brazil each year.
26183	9	Since the beginning of the war in Ukraine, Brazilian President Jair Bolsonaro said that his country would remain neutral. Bolsonaro met with Russian President Vladimir Putin in Moscow on February 16 and on that occasion said: “We are looking forward to collaborating [with Russia, ndr] in various fields. Defense, oil and gas, agriculture. Brazil is solidary with Russia.”
26183	11	As we can expect, this visit to Russia has been heavily criticized by the U.S. government because it took place in the middle of Western tensions with Russia on Ukraine. But Bolsonaro did not get back.
26183	13	Amazon is a huge bank of infinite natural resources for Brazilians. It has the most significant percentage of fresh water, precious minerals and oil globally. It is not surprising that the global elites appeal to environmental issues in an attempt to undermine Brazil’s sovereignty over the region. In fact, the environmentally protected areas in Brazil account for an impressive 25% of its entire territory, 50% of which in the Amazon alone. However, we are constantly watching a disinformation campaign on the deforestation of the Amazon.
26183	15	On the other hand, it is also true that Brazil still needs to import 97 percent of the approximately 10 million tons of potassium it uses annually for agricultural production, making it the world’s largest importer. So the fundamental question is: where could Brazil find more fertilizers?
26183	17	Potassium reserves in Brazil are found mainly in its indigenous lands in the Amazon region. According to Marcio Remédio, director of the Geological Survey of Brazil, a state company of the Ministry of Mining and Energy, “These reserves are of first order. They have the potential, if not more, of those of the Urals produced by Russia and Belarus, and also of the Saskatchewan in Canada.”
26183	19	"Only 3 percent of the Brazilian indigenous land is deforested: a rate lower than that of public and private land. The Brazilian Constitution defines indigenous lands as those traditionally occupied by the Brazilian Indians, as well as ""sources used for their production activities, those indispensable to the preservation of the environmental resources necessary for their well-being and their physical and cultural reproduction, according to their uses, customs and traditions."" This description is so broad that an eminent professor of constitutional law, Manoel G. Ferreira Filho, laughed saying that it would be easier if the Constitution had defined which land could occupy the non-Indian."
26183	21	The federal law in Brazil allows the exploration of mineral wealth in indigenous lands. A share of the benefit must be transferred to the relevant indigenous community that occupies the region, which cannot be removed from the ground unless in extraordinary cases of disasters or epidemics. Even so, these Indians retain the right to return to the land as soon as the risks cease.
26183	23	By signing an agreement with Russia, Brazil has prevented the extract of potassium that could harm the Amazon and violate indigenous rights; although it could potentially save the world from a catastrophic food crisis.
26183	25	“If Brazil should redimension next year due to the lack of fertilizers, it would be a bad news in case of a global food crisis,” says Joseph Schmidhuber, an economist who studied the impact of the food conflict, for the United Nations Food and Agriculture Organization.
26183	27	The war in Ukraine, combined with the economic sanctions of the West, threatened the world’s food security. These sanctions were intended to punish Russia for its invasion of Ukraine, but they are seriously threatening the world’s ability to feed.

26190	17	Economic pain in Europe
26190	19	According to analysts, the European economy could endure the greater weight of the recurring effects of the Ukrainian crisis in the form of even higher energy prices and a decrease in corporate confidence. Tian Dewen, Deputy Director of the Institute of European Studies at the Chinese Academy of Social Sciences, said the world is a global village where countries are economically interdependent and any crisis that occurs can affect people’s lives everywhere. An immediate impact of the Ukrainian crisis is the blow to Europe’s economic recovery on the background of the COVID-19 pandemic. “The impact of a conflict or a fire confrontation between Russia and Ukraine is intended to spread across Europe and beyond, with chain effects on the global economy,” Tian said. Russia is the world’s third-largest oil producer and one of the world’s leading natural gas exporters, while Ukraine is the world’s leading food exporter.
26190	21	Russia accounts for approximately 40% of the natural gas imports to the European Union and approximately 30% of its grain imports, according to Eurostat, the blockade statistical agency. The EU and the United States have imposed sanctions on the major Russian banks and its elites and frozen the central bank’s assets held outside the country. They also acted to remove some Russian banks from SWIFT, the payment system used for most international financial transactions. Tian said the energy issues will directly affect European countries, given the dependence of many of them on Russian supplies. Ukraine is a major transit hub for Russian oil and gas. Austria, Italy and Slovakia import natural gas from Russia, transported mainly through Ukraine. Part of the natural gas supplied by Russia also reaches Germany and Poland through Ukraine. Energy prices have steadily risen in Europe in the last year and the crisis in Ukraine will worsen the situation, Tian said. “For many countries, it is difficult to find short-term alternative energy solutions,” he said. Tian said that a feature of the EU economy is that, for the majority, its raw materials are supplied from outside the block, and local with high-intensity capital and technology are concentrated. Furthermore, its markets have no growth boost and many of the products in the region have to be sold outside Europe. “This is why uncertainty in the world economy will have a greater impact on the EU economy,” Tian said. “The burden of energy and raw materials prices and the lack of supply, as well as the global supply chains that have not fully recovered from the COVID-19 pandemic, are all negative factors for the recovery of the European economy.”
26190	23	Corporate trust: Tian said that investors and capital generally avoid exposure to conflicts and uncertainty will damage the trust and consumption of companies. This would have a great impact on the European economy, the researcher added.
26190	25	Chen Fengying, senior researcher on the world economy at China Institutes of Contemporary International Relations, said that, considering the EU’s dependence on Russian energy, there are indications that Western countries might not touch the energy sector in their actions against Moscow. But the conflict Russia-Ukraine will further fuel inflation in Europe. Apart from energy bills, food prices seem to be intended to rise, Chen added. According to the London consulting company Capital Economics, Russia and Ukraine together account for 25 to 30% of global grain exports and about 80% of global shipping of silk seeds. Chen said that many countries are already paying higher prices due to the conflict. In the EU, Germany is likely to suffer more. Its economy is growing more slowly than many other EU countries. Germany has a plan to give up nuclear energy by this year and has made rely on Russian energy. But on February 22, the country announced it would suspend the certification of the Nord Stream 2, which is worth about $11 billion. Chen said that if the conflict in Ukraine will slow down soon, there are reasons for optimism that its economic effects will gradually decrease.

I was surprised by the fact that that former rapper, who retained the appearance and very often the mental clothes of an Oxford student, has repeated for 13 times in a little more than 2 minutes that the vaccine is freedom, that is, has adopted one of those strategies to which the politicians who have little cultural baggage and who go before the crowd armed with a single phrase, who repeat to the infinite, as if the repetition revealed its strength and not, on the contrary, the argumentary weakness.

26208	11	Does the vaccine give us freedom? Yes and no.
26208	13	You may attribute to him the merit of giving us freedom if these vaccines had the ability to block infections, to prevent transmission.
26208	15	It is not so!
26208	17	The vaccine provides an infection protection, very good/good after the first 14 days of the inoculation, but decreases a few months from the 2nd dose, up to bleeding and even reversing, in the sense that fully vaccinated subjects become even less protected from infection than non-vaccinated. This paradoxal evolution is accelerated with the Omicron variant, especially in children and asymptomatics.
26208	19	It is not true that vaccine is freedom to go to school because for children from 5 to 11 years the risk of COVID infection is 40% higher for vaccinated than for non-vaccinated. (data of the ISS)
26208	21	It is not true that the vaccine is freedom to earn and work because from 18 to 69 years (the working age) the risk of COVID infection is 4 times higher in vaccinated with 3 doses than in non-vaccinated. (Data from the Ministry of Health) Three-vaccinated workers and entrepreneurs are more sensitive to the infection, and the party that would want to represent them should know that in Italy workers aged 40 to 59 have a 10% higher risk of getting sick if vaccinated with a full cycle than non-vaccinated (ISS data).

26208	25	It is not necessary to be doctors, it is enough to be politicians ready to examine vaccination policies, to ask questions about the fact that in June 2022, with a vaccine coverage among the highest in the world, we have more cases than last year, when the number of vaccinated was lower. 26208	27	Being prepared politicians also involves considering tools and strategies to prevent pandemic explosions: vaccines are not enough, we can’t always have the right vaccine available, and I say right intending a vaccine useful for the risky categories, but without guarantees that the benefits are actually greater than the risks.

Freedom and obligation are principles that presuppose a radically different view of the relationship between the state and the citizen: you can defend the greenpass and proclaim it a freedom instrument, repeating the phrase to the finest, but if we have to deal with the topic with a minimum of legal rigour then it is improbable to put together the two things because if you didn’t have the green pass didn’t work, which, if you allow me, was an even more sublime way of violating freedom in the field of vaccine choices: in this way you have even avoided to assume the responsibility of imposing the vaccine obligation, i.e. the responsibility of any negative effects of the short, medium or long vaccine period, which all drugs always have against collision effects, in terms of cost and benefits.

26209	1	Covid, a scientific article examines the evidence on the consequences of vaccines: “They are neither safe nor effective”
26209	3	In an article, published in the International Journal of Vaccine Theory, Practice, and Research, John W. Oller Jr., Emerite Professor of the University of New Mexico, and Daniel Santiago, a pharmacist from Orlando, Florida, examine “the evidence about the consequences of the worldwide experimental use of genetic vaccines apparently to stop the spread of the pathological conditions attributed to the SARS-CoV-2 virus and its variants.”
26209	5	Looking at the experimental data on anti-Covid injections, it turns out that these “vaccinations” are neither safe nor effective. For example, on the effectiveness of the reference doses, the British Health Service publication entitled “COVID-19 vaccine surveillance report week 42”, on page 23, states: “Recent observations from the surveillance data of the UK Health Safety Agency (UKHSA) have that the levels of N [natural instead of S, Spike] antibodies appear to be lower in individuals who counteract the infection after 2 doses of vaccination (UK Health Safety Agency, 2021). Similarly, a Pfizer study published on Lancet by (Tartof et al., 2021) the following change after the “complete vaccination” defined as “two doses of BNT162b2 with 7 or more days after the second dose: the effectiveness of the vaccine against infections for fully vaccinated was decreased with the increase of the time after vaccination, decreasing from 88% during the first month after the complete vaccination to 47% after 5 months”, read the article of Oller Jr. and Santiago.
26209	7	Another study, recently published by Cohn et al. (2022), suggests that submissions interfere with the inherent capacity of the organism after a SARS-CoV-2 infection to produce antibodies against the virus. One of theoretical possibilities is that people vaccinated against Covid may not produce antibodies against the nucleocapside protein, the virus worm, which is, in theory, an integral component necessary in the antibodies for a successful immune response to defeat the variants of Covid.”
26209	9	“It is already obvious that imperfect, non-sterilizing and non-neutralizing vaccines that can reduce symptoms, but do not stop infection or transmission, can surely create conditions that can make the disease more serious (Seneff and Nigh, 2021). It is imperative that doctors remain vigilant about the problems arising from experimental substances, regardless of the pervasive propaganda that claims that essentially all “vaccinations” are “safe and effective.” The evidence shows that some “vaccinations” can make a “vaccinated individual” more vulnerable to diseases rather than less. If the Vaccine Adverse Event Reporting System (VAERS) reports are reliable as they seem, anti-Covid injections are far the most dangerous ever produced in the history of vaccinology, or at least since the VAERS reporting system (Seneff et al., 2022) is in force,” reports Oller Jr. and Santiago.
26209	11	"“In a disappointing way, after billions of injections have been administered, according to Mitropoulos (2022): “There is an increasing percentage of deaths for Covid among vaccinated.” However, the public narrative returns to the starting point: the solution to deaths from the beginning of the Covid era is vaccinating, vaccinating, vaccinating. At the end of the article, we read that “the decline in immunity again highlights the urgency of encouraging older Americans and high-risk Americans to additional doses.” But how can the booster improve things if those who do more than one dose are actually becoming more vulnerable to Covid? And, as if it wasn’t enough, they’re more likely to die. Why do the individuals who made the references, according to the UK Health Safety Agency, actually have fewer antibodies against the disease and no more?"", the two authors of the article write."
26209	13	“What if the anti-Covid genetic vaccines were actually causing, not only the production of the Spike protein of SARS-CoV-2, but diseases and death? Something is killing many people who have already been vaccinated one or more times. Meanwhile, unvaccinated people, according to millions of people in the UK, die in a much lower number. This is evident by observing the UK Health Safety Agency’s weekly reports. There are also experimental findings that suggest that the anti-Covid vaccines themselves should be considered possible causal agents.”
26209	15	“Give the results of Aldén et al. 2022), Liu (2021) and Seneff et al. (2022), increasing evidence that the same anti-Covid injections not only create further disorders and pathological conditions, which could be weakening within a few weeks and even fatal, some of which appear suddenly, in anaphylactic convulsions or in forms of sudden death in perfectly healthy people (Heilman, 2022), should we not think of the possibility that the shocking number of damages and deaths by VAERS is actually caused by the anti-Covid vaccines?”, conclude Oller Jr. and Santiago.

26211	1	The Insect Allies Program – the Pandora Vase of DARPA
26211	3	The conflict between Russia and Ukraine has led to a global food crisis, in a period of climate change, pollution and other food supply threats. In the near future, food problems are likely to be a global problem, while conflicts resulting from “wares to harvests” will also become an international issue of great concern.
26211	5	Since 2016, the U.S. Advanced Military Research Institute (DARPA) has launched a defense program known as “Insect Allies,” which, according to him, would have to face the potential risks related to food supply. However, [in this program] the Pentagon uses insects to insert “genetically modified viruses” [in plant cell DNA], which could influence cultivation growth by altering the genes expressed by the plants themselves, according to the media reports.
26211	7	After the announcement, the plan had received widespread criticism from scientists and experts from all over the world, who had warned that “Insect Allies” could open a “Pandora bag” technology that could easily be tailored into weapons.
26211	9	Even the intentions of the Pentagon are not clear: is it really about saving mankind from hunger or, on the contrary, deliberately provoking a humanitarian crisis to pursue some “military goals”?
26211	11	According to experts heard by the Global Times, Insect Allies is turning this concern into a real danger. Why do we use insects as a carrier? Why do the U.S. build biological laboratories near other countries, like Russia? When Pandora’s vessel is open, it will follow a series of disasters,” an expert said.
26211	13	However, this is just the tip of the iceberg of a project that could easily translate into a biological weapon. In addition to the Insect Allies program, the United States has conducted biological experiments around the world in their famous “bio-laboratories,” ignoring the principles of safety and ethics and clearly violating the “Convention on biological weapons.”
26211	15	Insects become biological weapons
26211	17	The Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency (DARPA) is a U.S. Department of Defense’s research and development agency responsible for the development of high-tech military applications.
26211	19	Since DARPA announced the Insect Allies program, in the name of disasters prevention and increased agricultural productivity, the polemics around the proposal have never ceased.
26211	21	According to the DARPA website, the program pursues “escalable, easily implementable and generalizable controls” against “potential natural and engineered threats” to food supply, with the aim of preserving the U.S. agricultural system.
26211	23	According to DARPA, the program, “applying targeted therapies,” seeks to mitigate the impact of possible threats to the system of cultures, including those natural and those introduced by state or non-state actors,” which could quickly put national security at risk.
26211	25	According to DARPA, the Insect Allies program studies the possibility of modifying the genetic heritage of plants through carrier insects and plant viruses from them, involving three technical areas: viral manipulation, carrier insects optimization and selective genotherapy in mature plants.
26211	27	To this goal, the $45 million project has funded at least four research institutions, as by the media.
26211	29	According to the report, in 2017 one of Insect Allies experiments had involved corn and tomato plants and species of dispersive insects, including cavallets, white mosquitoes (aleurodids) and affids.
26211	31	However, the project and intentions of the DARPA did not convince the scientists. In April 2018, a Science article warned that insects that were selected in the Insect Allies program “will have been transformed into biological weapons.”
26211	33	“In case of success, the technique could be used by malicious actors to help spread diseases into almost all species of crops and destroy crops,” it read. “Research could constitute a violation of the Convention on biological weapons,” the Science article continues, citing European scientists.
26211	35	“The program could be widely perceived as an effort to develop to hostile purposes biological agents and their means of delivery,” the critics had observed.
26211	37	Also, according to the German Max Planck Institute, the Insect Allies program “may be easily misused for the development of biological weapons.”
26211	39	In a critical review published in January 2022 on the Society of Environmental Toxicology and Chemistry, scientists observed that “the combination of a genetic modification caused by viruses of plants grown on the field with genetically modified carrier insects poses a greater risk than the current use of genetically modified organisms.”
26211	41	In 2019, Forbes had included Insect Allies in the list of “the ethical problems of technology that we should all think about.” Will it motivate other countries to develop technology to defend themselves? I asked Forbes.
26211	43	Zhang Jie, an expert at the Plant Protection Institute of the Chinese Academy of Agricultural Sciences (CAAS), told Global Times that the possibility of using insects as a carrier of harmful bacteria and viruses to attack crops and cause a food crisis not only exists, but also has a wide margin of development.
26211	45	He said the three main crops – rice, grain and corn – all have viruses, bacteria or fatal fungi. In fact, targeted parasites, such as rice cicaline and grain grains, can carry various viruses to infect crops, causing enormous damage.
26211	47	“It would be lethal to turn a insect into a biological weapon, because, so far, the viruses in crops have been very difficult to control. Once an infected plant develops symptoms, it is almost impossible to save it. And the virus continues to vary, creating even more difficulties in prevention,” Zhang said.
26211	49	Zhou Huanbin, Zhang’s colleague who studies the genome editing, told Global Times that in the genome editing of crops it is necessary to follow a few principles, one of which is to minimize the risk of uncontrolled spread of genetically modified crops.
26211	51	All about the project’s controlability, Gregory Kaebnick, an ethic at the Hastings Center Institute of Bioethics Research in New York, has been quoted by AP for saying that once introduced into the fields, insects and microbes “may be impossible to remove.”
26211	53	Violations of the Convention on Organic Weapons
26211	55	The Insect Allies plan was labeled as “biological weapon” by Western scientists since the day it was announced, triggering acute discussions in Western academic circles and the media on the possibility that the plan could violate the United Nations Convention on Biological Weapons (BWC).
26211	57	Due to the extensive prohibition of the Convention on biological weapons, any biological research that is concerned must be plausibly justified as targeted for peaceful purposes. The Insect Allies program could be considered a violation of the Convention on Organic Weapons if the reasons presented by the DARPA were not plausible,” the article of the Max Planck Institute says.
26211	59	A milestone of the international control of biological weapons, the BWC was ready for the signature in 1972 and was entered into force in 1975, with more than 180 signatory states.
26211	61	The United States had initially pushed for the cancellation of the BWC and later became the only country to oppose the establishment of a multilateral verification mechanism for compliance with the Convention.
26211	63	“Using insects as carriers to spread diseases is a classic biological weapon,” said Silja Voeneky, a professor of international law at the University of Freiburg in Germany.
26211	65	According to Voeneky, in this program, the use of insects as a key element is “particularly alarming, because insects could be employed economically and surrettiously by malicious actors.”
26211	67	Chinese military expert Song Zhongping has called Insect Allies a “typical form of biological weapon.”
26211	69	“It could reduce harvests in targeted countries and artificially create food crises. In this way [the affected country] would lose its independence in the food industry and could become dependent on the U.S. food exports, including for genetically modified foods, which are part of the biological war,” Song said.
26211	71	Song believes that the U.S. should explain why in this research insects should be used as translators, especially because insects could peacefully spread viruses into cultures in other countries.
26211	73	“It’s not difficult to understand why the U.S. has established biological laboratories near rival nations, because only in this way laboratories can work with native species,” he said. “For example, it would be problematic if they brought American insects to an Ukrainian laboratory and then released them to Russia.”
26211	75	A long history of use of carrier insects
26211	77	The Insect Allies program is just one of many cases in which U.S. research has been accused of causing disastrous consequences worldwide, especially through the use of biological laboratories.
26211	79	The United States has openly admitted to managing 336 biological laboratories in 30 countries in the world, of which 26 in Ukraine. However, the signed contracts suggest that the United States has opened laboratories in 49 countries, many more than those officially recognized.
26211	81	The Pentagon has a long history of the use of insects as the carrier of diseases. According to a partially declassified 1981 report by the U.S. Army, U.S. scientists engaged in biological war had conducted several experiments on insects.
26211	83	In the 1980s, the U.S. Army’s Institute of Medical Research on Infectious Diseases had conducted experiments to verify “whether sand mosquitoes and pigs could be carrier of the Rift Valley Virus, Dengue, Chikungunya and Eastern Equal Encephalitis.”
26211	85	In the same decade, as part of a U.S. military operation called May Day, in the state of Georgia the Aedes Aegupti worms had been dispersed by land methods. The bears would be the carriers of dengue, chikungunya and the Zika virus.
26211	87	Gaytandzhieva also revealed that the Pentagon would conduct entomological war tests in countries such as Georgia and Russia.
26211	89	In 2014, the Lugar Center, built in the United States, near Tbilisi, the capital of Georgia, had been equipped with an insect research facility and had launched a project called “Raising Awareness about Barcoding of Sand Flies in Georgia and Caucasus.”
26211	91	As a result, since 2015, Tbilisi has been infected by ‘punging’ mosques that had developed an atypical behavior to local species, such as being able to survive the whole year in closed environments and be highly cold-resistant.
26211	93	Furious mosques have also been found in the nearby Russian region of Daghestan.
26211	95	Furthermore, while conducting research on viruses and deadly bacteria, the United States had not been able to guarantee the safety of its biological laboratories. In 2015, the Pentagon had admitted that in 2003, live antrace samples were mistakenly sent from the Dugway Proving Ground military base near Salt Lake City, in Utah, to all 50 states and to nine countries, including the United Kingdom, South Korea and Germany.

2622	1	The Covid is the Point of the Iceberg.
2622	3	Covid was just the beginning. Climate change could lead to 15,000 new viruses by 2070. The scenario is published in the journal Nature, a result of the research coordinated by biologist Colin Carlson of the American Georgetown University.
2622	5	From puppets to many other species of mammals, to birds. There are many species known to be viral carriers and that, on the push of climate change, could push themselves to occupy areas different from those in which they normally live. This could lead to the fact that the viruses of these animals can in this way get in touch with us through what is called the “ship of species”. It is the virus that moves until it can attack a new species, in a domino effect that could reach man. What would have happened to Covid to understand us.
2622	7	The problem is climate change and the increase in temperature. With only two degrees from the current temperature, 15,000 new viruses could emerge by 2070. There are currently 10,000 in circulation. It’s much closer than you imagine, therefore, the link between climate change and the appearance of viruses that could carry diseases you’ve ever seen.
2622	9	The climate, the research authors find, has the potential to become a training force in viral transmission between different species. This could increase the risk of transmission of infectious diseases to humans, in a vision in line with the so-called One Health, the approach that connects animal health with that of humans and the environment.
2622	11	In addition to infectious diseases for humans, future viruses may be a threat to animal health. They can cause harmful epidemics for farms. The research was based on the analysis of how the geographical areas currently populated by 3,870 species of mammals could change in relation to several scenarios from here to 2070.
2622	13	Applying a pattern on the transmission of viruses between species to a subset of 3,139 animals, the researchers elaborated the forecast on future opportunities for the exchange of viruses between species. Events of such biological mixture are possible everywhere in the world, but are concentrated in areas densely populated by humans, such as tropical Africa and Southeast Asia.
2622	15	Again, the research authors note, the “protagonists” of these contaminations might be the pipistrels, which constitute the natural reservoir of viruses potentially capable of becoming transmitted to humans. Preventing the spread of new viruses requires capillary surveillance of areas where different species may live together.
2622	17	For research authors it is important to push from now on to understand how important it is to combine virological surveillance with the assessment of changes in the new areas occupied by species due to climate change. This is true in tropical regions, where most infectious diseases can be transmitted from animals to humans.

On the right of the tomb is placed the second monument composed of a travertine cage and a marble chip. 2624	3	The survey of 5,000 Italian students carried out by the Adolescence Laboratory and the Iard Institute: among the reasons of anxiety also the economic impacts, but not the arrival of refugees.
2624	5	The war in Ukraine scares the boys, who already had their fears related to the pandemic. Eight out of ten between the ages of 13 and 19 fear Italy’s involvement in the conflict or even the outbreak of the Third World War, but among the reasons of anxiety there are also the economic impacts that we may have. They are not worried about the arrival of tens of thousands of refugees from war zones to Italy and have great empathy for the suffering of the Ukrainian people. The answers are referred to the national survey on the lifestyle of teenagers living in Italy conducted annually by the Milan Association “Laboratorio Adolescenza” and the Research Institute IARD. The survey is normally conducted on a national sample of 3,500 students aged between 13 and 19 years, but this year the sample was 5,000 students.
2624	7	So, so much fear and suffering for the strikes of civilians in Bucha and in other centers around Kiev. 2624	9	The investigation began a few days after the outbreak of the war in Ukraine, so it was possible to ask some questions aimed at understanding whether and how certain aspects related to the war could create alarms and concerns among teenagers.
2624	11	The fear that Italy will enter war is three out of four, while eight out of ten boys are afraid of a third world war. Then there are economic concerns, eight out of ten know that in family you have to save because the costs increase. Only 13 percent say they are very concerned about the arrival of the refugees, in fact the majority – one in two of the 5,000 children interviewed – is rather impressed by the pain of the people attacked by the Russians, a pain that is perceived by looking at the images of the bombings and the devastations that followed.
2624	13	“The concern of adolescents is very high, in all aspects considered, with percentages that are generally between 80 and 90%. The humanitarian aspects (the suffering of the Ukrainian people and the involvement of civilians in the war) are – along with the fear of economic impacts that we might have from the war – the areas to which the concern is greater.
2624	15	It is interesting to observe – but it is linked with the emotional involvement towards the suffering of the Ukrainian people – that the absolute majority does not consider worrying even the possible numerous arrival of refugees from the war zones. The level of concern depends on the age (increased by the age) but, above all, the gender. Girls are averagely more concerned than men (the only exception is the predictable flow of refugees in Italy) and even among those who say they’re “occupied/or” the degree of concern is greater among girls.”
2624	17	“A further aspect discussed in the survey concerned the overall vision of the future (and therefore not specifically referred to the war) by teenagers. The absolute majority has a generally negative view (occupied or uncertain). Only 11% of girls and 18% of men call themselves optimists. 26244	1	The European Commission's REPowerEu plan - Europe
26244	3	The EU Court of Auditors announced today that the European Commission’s REPowerEU plan was presented in mid-May to accelerate the reduction of dependence on fossil fuels from Russia and increase the resilience of the EU energy system. According to the analysis carried out by the Court, of the 210 billion additional funding that the Commission estimates will be activated by the REPowerEU, the ones that will be directly and actually made available by the plan will only be 20 billion.
26244	5	"The rest of the planned investments are ""out of the Commission's control and depend on the willingness of the Member States to use the remaining loans of the Recovery and Resilience Facility (RRF) or to withdraw funds from other EU policies, in particular those for cohesion and rural development."" As a result, the Court warns that the total amount of funding actually available may not be sufficient to cover the estimated investment need. ""The invasion of Ukraine by Russia has shed reflectors on our dependence on the imports of gas, oil and coal, and the EU had absolutely to act and respond quickly to the increasing concerns regarding energy security,"" said Ivana Maletic, the court member responsible for the opinion."
26244	7	"""But the Court has noted that REPowerEU, in its current form, may not be able to quickly identify and implement EU strategic projects that have a maximum and immediate impact on the energy security and independence of the Union. A risk, the one highlighted by Meletic, fueled by a ""series of incompatibilities"" found by the Court in the concept of the REPowerEU plan. Incoherences arising mainly from alleged synergies between the plan itself, focused on the Union as a whole, and the RRF, that is, the instrument on the basis of the Pnrr and therefore declined on the basis of national projects. All elements that, according to the Court, could severely limit the financing of cross-border projects and those with the greatest potential to contribute to the security and energy independence of the EU."

26247	1	Covid Animal Party Wuhan Market: Studies Cancel Doubts
26247	3	Analysis of the beginning of the pandemic in China
26247	5	The covid 19 started from the living animals sold in the Wuhan market, China, at the end of 2019. This is the conclusion to which the authors of the studies published in 2 articles on the journal Science. The analysis coordinated by Professor Michael Worobey - Director of the Department of Ecology and Biology of the University of Arizona - involved experts of various nationalities and produced the texts that actually exclude any alternative hypothesis for the origin of the pandemic. According to the authors, the virus's transition from animals to humans occurred in two distinct events, in the Huanan market - in Wuhan - at the end of 2019.
26247	7	One of the studies examined the localization of the first known cases of Covid 19, combining the information with the results of the anaalysis on tampons taken from surfaces and caves in different sections of the market. The other study focused on the genomic sequences of SARS-CoV-2 after the analysis of samples provided by patients positive results during the first weeks of pandemic in China.
26247	9	The first study, conducted by Worobey and Kristian Andersen at the Scripps Research Institute in San Diego, California, examined the geographical model of Covid 19 cases in the first month of the epidemic, December 2019. Scientists have been able to determine the position of almost all 174 cases of Covid 19 identified by the World Health Organization in that month.
26247	11	Analysis showed that the cases concentrated around the Huanan market, while the subsequent infections had a broad spread in the city of Wuhan, inhabited by 11 million people. In particular, the researchers found that a surprising percentage of the first patients affected by Covid without any direct link to the market – not workers or customers – was still located in areas near the commercial structure.
26247	13	“This reinforces the idea that the market was the epicenter of the epidemic,” says Worobey, explaining that sellers and workers were infected for the first time and actually started a chain of infections.
26247	15	“In a city that extends over 5,000 square kilometers, the area with greater probability of hosting someone’s home among the world’s first infected was in a perimeter of a few streets, with the Huanan market right inside,” says Worobey.
26247	17	Scientists also examined samples taken from the market surfaces, such as floors and rubber, after the structure was closed. The positive results samples for SARS-CoV-2 were associated with bankers selling living wild animals.
26247	19	The researchers found that mammals now known to be susceptible to infection – red wolves, tails and prophins – were sold alive in the Huanan market in the weeks prior to the registration of the first cases among men.
26247	21	“The mountain events remain dark, but our analysis of the available evidence suggests that the pandemic is derived from human infections from animals in sale to the wholesale sea fruit market in Huanan at the end of November 2019,” Andersen, co-author of both studies, summarized.
26247	23	The second study, a genetic analysis from the first cases, was co-directed by Jonathan Pekar and Joel Wertheim of the University of California, San Diego, and Marc Suchard of the University of California, Los Angeles.
26247	25	The researchers found that the pandemic, which initially involved two slightly different SARS-CoV-2 lignages, was probably derived from at least two human infections caused by animals in the Huanan market in November 2019 and in December 2019. The most likely hypothesis is that the two lignages have been transferred from animals to humans in two distinct episodes.

26280	3	The Cnr Hydrogeological Protection Research Institute in a study shows how climate change affects high-percentage environments. The “catalogue” of events.
26280	5	In 85 percent of cases high rate instability events are associated with a temperature anomaly, and the role of positive temperature anomalies increases from spring to winter, and with the share and volume of the event.
26280	7	These are the conclusions of an analysis conducted by the Research Institute for Hydrogeological Protection of the National Research Council (Cnr-Irpi) which, in a note, illustrates the tools used for the monitoring of glacial masses and the related unstability phenomena, such as the recent ice collapse of the Marmolada.
26280	9	The presence of glacial masses has always been associated with the possibility of unstabilities potentially dangerous for human activities, such as the large collapse of glacial fronts and sudden full glacial.
26280	11	The study of instability
26280	13	Cnr-Irpi has been working for more than thirty years in the field of studies relating to the documentation of the unstability phenomena in the ice area, with particular reference to the characterization of the dynamics of the glaciers, to the reconstruction of the events of the past and to the analysis of the factors involved in the emergence of unstability phenomena.
26280	15	Thanks to the knowledge and expertise acquired in national and international research projects and scientific collaborations (such as GLACIORISK and GLARISKALP), the Cnr-Irpi has contributed to the implementation of the only existing European-specific ice risk database (http://www.nimbus.it/glaciorisk/gridabasemainmenu.asp) and the drafting of the International Guidelines for the definition and mitigation of ice risks (https://www.gaphaz.org/).
26280	17	One of the most important challenges today is the understanding of the impact of climate change on glacial masses and their instability, also considered the increasing frequency of high-cost environments and thus the increasing related risks.
26280	19	“Ice instability phenomena are increasing worldwide, including in Italy, but for statistically-based conclusions it is necessary the consolidation of national and international strategies for the systematic documentation of this type of phenomena,” explains Marta Chiarle, researcher of the Institute.
26280	21	To contribute to the knowledge in this field, the Cnr-Irpi has a high mountain research focus that concerns both the role of climate and geomorphological evolution in the predisposition and injection of instability processes in cryospheric environments (nees, glaciers and permafrosts), and the integration of high-frequency monitoring systems for the characterization of instability phenomena in the ice area.
26280	23	The “Instability”
26280	25	“As for the first aspect – adds Chiarle – we have implemented and placed online a record of high-percentage instability events (https://geoclimalp.irpi.cnr.it/catasto-frane/): the data set analysis highlighted how in 85% of cases the events are associated with some temperature anomaly and how the role of positive temperature anomaly increases from spring to winter, and with the share and volume of the event.”
26280	27	As regards the monitoring systems, Daniele Giordan explains that the research activities carried out in collaboration with the Safe Mountain Foundation and the Austin Valley Region have led to the construction of the Open Sky Laboratory of the Grandes Jorasses, where the Planpincieux glacier and the Whymper seracus are followed with a worldwide unique monitoring system.
26280	29	This monitoring system has enabled in the years to acquire a significant amount of information on the dynamics of the Planpincieux and the Grandes Jorasses glaciers, on which it was based the development of a risk management protocol on the possible collapse of significant portions of the two glaciers.
26280	31	The researcher Daniele Giordan adds “the open-air laboratory of the Grandes Jorasses is a virtuous example of collaboration between research and territory management institutions; born from a need for civil protection, the laboratory is also a space where to do high-level research based on the most technologically advanced systems, whose results are used in the development of new monitoring techniques and in the irrobustering of the site management protocol.”
26280	33	The director Tommaso Moramarco, director of the Cnr-Irpi, concludes: “The Cnr-Irpi therefore has a know-how and data set on glacial risks of fundamental importance to assess the danger in high mountains. Such knowledge may be useful to the country for the drafting of national guidelines for the assessment of glacial risks, with particular attention to the effects of climate change in place, to the training of citizens and to the disclosure, in order to know and live the high mountains safely.
26280	35	This is added to the scientific and technological know-how of the Cnr-Irpi that put it at the forefront in the monitoring of unstable glacial bodies. All this knowledge is made available to the decision-making bodies and the government of the territory to do everything possible so that tragedies like the Marmolada do not have to repeat.”

26288	3	Climate-sensitive diseases account for approximately 70% of global deaths, of which cardiovascular diseases make up the highest percentage (32.8%). From fire to heat waves, the data does not change. In 2020, Italy saw one of the highest increases in temperature throughout Europe, with +1,54 C compared to the average of the period 1961-1990 and continues to surheat faster than the global average. 26293	1	Sustainable Finance and EU Taxonomy: What Changes?
26293	3	The taxonomy of the EU changes the sustainable finance. Let’s see how
26293	5	The European Parliament promoted the Sustainability Taxonomy introduced by the European Commission, led by Ursula von der Leyen, in early July. With this move, the Strasbourg semi-cycle has led to the entry into force of a proposal that aims to track a net hole. Giving, therefore, a definitive picture of what is considered functional for the sustainable development of the Old Continent and what does not belong to that scope in the economic activities promoted within the Old Continent. This also has great impacts on sustainable finance, a field where Brussels wants to play as a protagonist.
26293	7	The impact will be significant, in particular, in ensuring that companies and financial institutions that promote the issuance of sustainable bonds, “green” products and budgets dedicated to the ESG criteria have an increased degree of uniformity. It emerges from the Tasonomy the desire to strengthen two European plans related to the Sustainable Finance: on the one hand, the Sustainable Finance Action Plan; on the other, the complementary Sustainable Finance Disclosure Regulation, which aims to promote an increasing level of transparency. Since 6 July, the day of approval, only economic activities that openly contribute to one or more of the six environmental objectives are defined as sustainable in a unique and unambiguous form. These include: climate change mitigation of the economic system; adaptation of strategic sectors to climate change; protection of marine and water resources; transition to a circular economy; pollution prevention; protection and restoration of biodiversity and ecosystems.
26293	9	"Now for the operators the biggest burden will be to understand how to optimize feedback on the topic. In Italy, the Forum for Sustainable Finance has taken a position since the beginning of the reform process on the field of the new Taxonomy and ""monitors carefully the progressive development of the European Taxonomy, which is a valid tool for the classification of sustainable investments to indicate greater transparency and disclosure. This is an important measure that, however, will be able to deploy its positive potential if it takes into account the boundaries and will increase the opportunities for sustainable finance,” said Forum Secretary-General, Francesco Bicciato."
26293	11	In the recent study Taxonomy of the EU and other regulations on sustainable finance: implications for financial operators, the Forum for Sustainable Finance emphasized that, in this perspective, it is necessary to have “clear and consistent data” to make the difference to allow an enterprise a precise reporting of its activities. In this sense, it will serve to maintain the current level of deformity in the burden imposed on each enterprise in relation to sustainability: on the initiative of the European Parliament of the Brothers of Italy Raffaele Stancanelli last spring the Corporate Sustainability Due Diligence (Csdd) directive with which the EU wants to complete the set of policies aimed at regulating the energy transition agenda to normalize the management of the sectors reconditioned under the criteria of environmental, social and governance sustainability, prodomic to Tassonomy, was amended to promote small and medium-sized enterprises. CSDD essentially provides several levels of obligation for enterprises in reporting sustainability budget activities that will be more stringent only for enterprises with at least 500 employees and 140 million euros of revenue.
26293	13	"Thus, the nature of taxonomy is best perimetrated and, above all, the strongest link is offered to binding, in substantial form, transparency on sustainability and financial transparency, which is especially required to those companies that point on the ESG criteria to go on the capital markets. Companies covered by Taxonomy will have to account for the turnover, capital investments and operating costs related to the activities that are part of Taxonomy and this, noted by the Sustainable Finance Forum study, can allow investors to ""analize the companies taking into account their environmental impact and the decarbonization projects. Furthermore, greater availability of information will support both the self-evaluations of companies regarding their risks and climate impacts, and the investor dialogue with invested companies, and will allow greater transparency regarding the financial instruments that are proposed to sustainability goals.” First among all green bonds that can be issued only if really such, therefore well defined in the objectives and prospects. But in this perspective, Taxonomy can also contribute significantly to the fight against corporate greenwashing. It is a European priority on which taxonomy offers a further spoon. The game will be complex and companies will definitely have to be careful about internal accounts to return only what is relevant to the activities of the Taxonomy. But it represents the first step towards a common standard that is vital to obtain when it comes to sustainable finance and investment on the subject."

26297	3	Globalization, as we know it, is intended to change with the pandemic before and the Russian war in Ukraine after. From supply chains to supply chains
26297	5	The Covid-19 pandemic, the severe interruptions of maritime transportation (such as the case of the Ever Given ship crushed in the Suez channel or carried them containers for the war in Ukraine), the rise of populist nationalism and the growing tensions between China and all its main commercial partners, led experts to proclaim the death of globalization. However, what is expected is not a less globalized world.
26297	7	The advent of the Coronavirus demonstrated more than other events the fragility of the global supply chains and printed a substantial acceleration to the so-called “deglobalization” trend, a term that technically means “the overcoming of globalization through the incentive of local markets.”
26297	9	Deglobalization and slowbalization
26297	10	Globalization should therefore not be understood as something extreme, a deflagration of globalization that has characterized the world economy for 40 years, but as what the Economist has called slowbalisation, or a slowdown in the trends of economic and financial integration between countries.
26297	12	Instead of withdrawing, globalization is taking a form for broad traits unknown even to analysts.
26297	14	“In just over three decades, millions of families around the world have been able to buy cars and TVs, clothes and air conditioners for the first time. Many of these consumer goods are mainly produced by “low-cost” factory in Asian countries, but they use resources ( raw materials) from other countries: this is the type of activity that we think about when we talk about “globalization”. Since production has moved from Europe, North America and Japan to China, Vietnam and Indonesia, the prices of many consumer goods are today lower than they were at the beginning of the century,” said Mohamed EL-Erian, president of the Queen’s College in London, who held the International Monetary Fund a conference entitled “Navigating the New Normal in Industrial Countries”.
26297	16	To decree the beginning of globalization is therefore the disappearance of these trends that supported globalization. In North America, Europe and Asia, the population is growing slowly – or decreasing – and aging rapidly. In almost all middle and high-income countries, fewer new families are formed and older families buy fewer goods and are more likely to spend on travel and vacation.
26297	18	Efficiency vs Resilience
26297	19	The pandemic has only been the last – although the most impressive – of a series of events adversely to the globalized model. There are obvious geopolitical issues, of which the war in Ukraine does not end. But at the center of globalization there are the geopolitical tensions between China and the United States and, in general, the dependence relationship (including Europe) that has established itself with China, the “world factory” for antonomy: “In addition to these difficulties of economic policy, there is then the topic of energy, which not only translates into the growth of the accounts for private citizens, but has significant consequences on the production and costs of companies. In addition, it tends to forget how disruptions in the supply chain due to natural disasters, caused by the climate crisis, result in billion-dollar losses in the form of production stops and lack of revenue,” writes Marc Levinson, economist and historian of Economist and Independent who on the topic just published the book “The Box”.  This is due to the complexity behind the supply chains, so the managers themselves have difficulty monitoring their developments, if not in certain cases, to have full knowledge of them, making them a lack of preparation in terms of risk management, i.e. risk management.
26297	21	The Role of Technology in Globalization: No, It's Not What You Think
26297	22	Even technology – it seems a paradox, but you’ll see that it’s not so – is leading globalization, because it limits trade. For example, economist Marc Levinson said in an article on the latest May issue of the Economist: “In 2021, all automotive manufacturers have announced significant investments in electric cars. It may be a great news for the environment, but it will have a negative and in many cases fatal impact on the tens of thousands of companies that are part of the supply chains of the automotive houses: the average electric vehicle has several thousand pieces less than a vehicle with internal combustion of similar sizes.” But there is not only this case, rather told by the newspapers also in Italy: consumers, around the world, no longer need stereo installations – the market increasingly more than niche – when they can buy streaming music services on their smartphones. As for, in many countries more than a fifth of the investment is currently destined to research, software and other intangible expenses rather than to machinery and equipment. Updating industrial facilities often means downloading software instead of replacing hardware, which further hinderes factory sales. Innovations such as cloud computing allow to share computers as well as bike sharing allows people to share bicycles, limiting the overall demand for this type of material assets.
26297	24	Reshoring, the “Great Return”
26297	25	A passage in the wisdom of Professor Mohamed EL-Erian makes an effective summary of how globalization is changing “switching” towards “deglobalization”: “Global production is becoming gradually less important for the global economy, even for this reason it is seen a phenomenon of reduction of labor employed in factories in those countries – often in Southeast Asia – where the production chains in recent years had been delocalized. As a step towards this phenomenon, we are witnessing the exponential growth of automation that eliminates (or slows down) the few signals of “return” (reshoring) of industrial production, from “low wage” Asian countries to “high wage” in Europe and North America. On the contrary, EL-Erian believes, there are considerable evidence that manufacturers and retailers are trying to keep the risks under control, diversifying the sources of supply of key components and finished products, instead of producing everything in giant plants located in Asia. For a multinational company, it is likely that an export-oriented factory to Mexico or Morocco will integrate, rather than replace, a factory in China.”
26297	27	Is globalization really over?
26297	28	Globalization is in decline and governments (including the Italian) are granting subsidies or eriding customs barriers to protect the markets – after the trumpet policies, the last case is India that blocks grain and sugar exports – to the benefit of domestic producers. But if the globalization of manufacturing production has a lower weight than before, the globalization of products that physically do not cross the boundaries is more important than ever. “Today – concludes Levinson – banks sign loans in one country, approve bureaucratic practices in another and refund payments in a third. Industrial companies and software companies give life to research centers around the world, turning many individual research projects into international initiatives. It will be interesting to observe the new space race, which is going forward according to the logic of globalization. Today, finally, a British book publisher can easily address a reporter in Pakistan and a film can be filmed and produced in Chile and sold from or on streaming platforms, or on them, anywhere, translating dialogues into multiple languages, also using artificial intelligence.
